  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9c37eae1-7a29-4301-bc17-2f93e7828494'

  <span id="freeText9413211173790364226" style="display:none">Kapan terakhir kali kita memeluk ayah kita? Menatap wajahnya, lantas bilang kita sungguh sayang padanya? Kapan terakhir kali kita bercakap ringan, tertawa gelak, bercengkerama, lantas menyentuh lembut tangannya, bilang kita sungguh bangga padanya?<br /><br />Inilah kisah tentang seorang anak yang dibesarkan dengan dongeng-dongeng kesederhanaan hidup. Kesederhanaan yang justru membuat ia membenci ayahnya sendiri. Inilah kisah tentang hakikat kebahagiaan sejati. Jika kalian tidak menemukan rumus itu di novel ini, tidak ada lagi cara terbaik untuk menjelaskannya.<br /><br />Mulailah membaca novel ini dengan hati lapang, dan saat tiba di halaman terakhir, berlarilah secepat mungkin menemui ayah kita, sebelum semuanya terlambat, dan kita tidak pernah sempat mengatakannya.<br /><br /><br />Tere-Liye adalah pengarang beberapa novel dengan rating tinggi di website para pencinta buku <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com">www.goodreads.com</a>. Tere-Liye banyak menghabiskan waktu untuk melakukan perjalanan, mencoba memahami banyak hal dengan melihat banyak tempat. Selamat membaca novel kecil ini.<br /><br />Setamat membaca buku ini, satu hal yang pasti nyata: saya menangguk banyak kearifan di kedalaman cerita.<br />--A. Fuadi, Penulis Trilogi Negeri 5 Menara<br /><br />Sungguh Tere-Liye berhasil menggugah saya sebagai pembaca sekaligus seorang anak dari seorang ayah yang sangat saya banggakan. A must read.<br />--Amang Suramang, Penggerak di Goodreads Indonesia<br /><br />Isinya tak hanya menggugah dan membuat haru, tapi membuat kita merasa perlu meneguhkan kembali keyakinan dan kecintaan pada keluarga. Salut atas novel ini!<br />--Arwin Rasyid, Presiden Direktur Bank CIMB-Niaga<br /><br />Novel ini dapat menjadi langkah awal untuk menata ulang konsep budi pekerti di negeri ini.<br />--Muliaman D. Hadad, Deputi Gubernur Bank Indonesia</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amirul Adlil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amirul Adlil" href="/user/show/57275132-amirul-adlil">Amirul Adlil</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684249501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777843264599504963">This book tells a story about a kid and his father. The father has a unique way to educate his only child, by telling him his 'own' fairy tales-like adventure stories. As the result, the child grew up with what it takes to become a good person; he got patience, honesty, determination, and is living a humble life. He believed all the stories his father told were true, until an incident happens and makes him doubting the stories, and even his father.<br/><br/>This book has a slow and calm plot, so readers s</span>
  <span id="freeText14777843264599504963" style="display:none">This book tells a story about a kid and his father. The father has a unique way to educate his only child, by telling him his 'own' fairy tales-like adventure stories. As the result, the child grew up with what it takes to become a good person; he got patience, honesty, determination, and is living a humble life. He believed all the stories his father told were true, until an incident happens and makes him doubting the stories, and even his father.<br /><br />This book has a slow and calm plot, so readers should have patience when reading it. It makes this book a good choice to read in break time, for example while drinking tea at dawn. While you are following the kid's character development (to a grown up man), sometimes you will be invited to see the kid's childhood, where his father told him stories and then the plot goes back to a problem the kid facing, the problem that is relevant to the story. Although there are more than two characters in this books, the book only focus on the kid and his father and the bond between them. The other characters are just supportive characters, but the author managed to turn their appearance as a tool to makes the bond between those two iconic characters clearer.<br /><br />My conclusion, this book is a good choice to read in your break time. If you have problems with your father, and I know every boys have it, or if you can not forgive your father for some reasons, you can try to read this book and see if this book can make things better. Also, try not to cry after you finished this book, I challenge you.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706030791?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia " href="/user/show/4677384-lia">Lia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706030791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18390110861029433985">What I found one of the differences between east and western stories that the eastern authors like to crammed and imparted as much as wisdom of life as they can - sometimes can feel too condescending almost choked their readers with no room of escapism. This one is no different. It's my first introduction with the author recommended by someone during my short visit to Indonesia. It's a good story though not believable. How could someone so intrigued with the truth of his father's fairytale yet n</span>
  <span id="freeText18390110861029433985" style="display:none">What I found one of the differences between east and western stories that the eastern authors like to crammed and imparted as much as wisdom of life as they can - sometimes can feel too condescending almost choked their readers with no room of escapism. This one is no different. It's my first introduction with the author recommended by someone during my short visit to Indonesia. It's a good story though not believable. How could someone so intrigued with the truth of his father's fairytale yet never that curious about his parents past life? How can you say the father's fairytale had shaped the boy become a high morale man while still has a heart to evict his old man in the middle of the night under the rain? These were all thrown in for a good drama, to get that climax. The ending is soppy and no brainer. I would put a higher score if the author left it there - That those stories are all fictions or exaggeration of true events, so the boy can learn some morals. But then it made no different with Big Fish. But then again, like it or not, this is his stories, his ending. I put 3 stars as I actually can really relate to the main character, I grew up with a father just like that - only the ending was my own version. I know my old dad loves of the art of storytelling, can accept and still love his fairytales as I grew up, can never imagine I could threw him out of my house and will never crossed my mind to call him a liar. Nevertheless this won't put me off to pick up the next book of the author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18390110861029433985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12462940629583684016" style="display:none">I didn't finish the book. Sorry... I keep waiting and waiting to find out whether the dad was lying or not. While the boy (now a grown up man and married) thinks that his father told lies through his stories, the father (now a grandfather) keeps on telling the same stories to his grandchildren.<br /><br />I read until half book, and still couldn't find out whether the man's thinking of his father being a liar is true or false. I should have known from the title that the father is not a liar. But how did the man find out about it? I want to know. But I still couldn't manage to finish the book. Maybe the time is just not right. <br /><br />From what I've read, the way the author tells his story is amazing, as usual. He has a way with words and rich with vocabulary. I like his style. And perhaps I would try to read the book in the future, now that I've bought the book for the library collection. <br /><br />Next, I want to try reading Kau, Aku, dan Sepucuk Angpau Merah. My friend recommends this, and I also bought it for the library collection. This one thicker than the last one, but I hope I could find the time during Dec holiday to finish it. *hwaiting!*<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Dl3ofZ6WySNFGo26Gn1PnezUL6neNL7eI91Ks3p9yvOsDIb42vZ/QZi2SJnljUwtwvpu90JTxhfnHMmSiRevPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xx2bCMviKkK2I5ydXx4w5d5sPftAFPehLJjh7GWj32NlTPWNj4KcIGuPWb6g7jNV8EJ8pdxzj2joWWLNlsm6rA==')})
  }
